This results in a harmonious individual. The loss of regular defense qi causes those with abundant flesh to have a distended belly, the fleshy ones to appear large from top to bottom, while the fatty ones cannot grow large despite having fat. Defense qi governs the area between skin, flesh, tendons, and bones, floating and sinking in various depths, each in its place. If it is solely concentrated in the space between skin and flesh, leading to a distended belly and large form, or sinking deeply into the tendons and bones so that fat cannot grow large, these are all disturbances of the defense qi. Therefore, the floating and sinking, the deep and shallow, cannot be fully exhaustively categorized; adjustments to qi are made according to changes, referred to as the superior practitioner.)

    In the chapter on the Five Prohibitions:

    Stagnation that does not shift, ruptured flesh, body heat, and an irregular pulse are considered adverse conditions.

    (Note: Stagnation that does not shift, ruptured flesh, and body heat occur when dampness injures the form, leading to prolonged transformation into heat. An irregular pulse signifies the failure of the spleen and stomach qi.)[21p]

    　　　　　刺节真邪篇

    　　虚邪之入于身也深，寒与热相搏，久留而内着。寒胜其热，则骨疼肉枯；热胜其寒，则烂肉腐肌为脓，内伤骨。内伤骨为骨蚀。有所疾前筋，筋屈不能伸，邪气居其间而不反，发于筋溜，有所结，气归之，卫气留之，不得反，津液久留，合而为肠溜，久者数岁乃成。以手按之柔，已有所结，气归之，津液留之，邪气中之，凝结日以易甚，连以聚居，为昔瘤。以手按之坚，有所结，深中骨，气因于骨，骨与气并，日以益大，则为骨疽。有所结，中于肉，宗气归之，邪留而不去，有热则化而为脓，无热则为肉疽。凡此数气者，其发无常处，而有常名也。　　【注　寒与热搏者，形中之阴阳二气也。盖形舍气，气归形，形气之相合也。是以伤形则病气，伤气则病形。结气归之者，寒热相搏之气，归于邪留之形所也。凡此数气者，其发无定处，而有肉枯、骨蚀、筋溜、昔瘤之定名也。】[22p]

    The True Evil of Pathogenic Factors

    The intrusion of void and evil into the body is profound; cold and heat clash, lingering long and taking root within. If cold predominates over heat, the bones ache and the flesh withers; if heat predominates over cold, the flesh rots, the muscles decay into pus, leading to internal bone injury. Internal bone injury results in bone erosion.

    If there is an affliction in the tendons, they become bent and cannot straighten; the pathogenic energy resides within and does not retreat, causing swelling in the tendons, creating knots, and the vital energy converges, while the defending energy remains, unable to retreat. If bodily fluids linger long, they combine to form intestinal channels, and it often takes several years for this to manifest.

    If one presses on it gently and a knot is already present, the vital energy converges, and the bodily fluids remain, while the pathogenic energy is trapped inside; as it condenses, over time it becomes more severe, congregating into what is termed a 'historic lump.'

    If one presses and it is firm, with a knot that penetrates deep into the bones, the energy emanates from the bones; as the bones and energy merge, it increases daily, resulting in bone abscesses. If a knot is within the flesh, the ancestral energy converges, and the evil lingers without dispersing; if there is heat, it transforms into pus, and without heat, it results in flesh abscesses.

    All these various pathogenic energies do not emerge from fixed locations, yet they bear consistent names. [Note: The clash of cold and heat refers to the yin and yang energies within the body. The essence it's about the body housing energy; when the essence is injured, the energy suffers, and vice versa. The converging of energy signifies the clashing of cold and heat, which becomes trapped within the form of evil. Thus, these various energies manifest unpredictably, yet they have established names such as flesh withering, bone erosion, tendon swelling, and historic lumps.][22p]

    　　　　　九宫八风篇

    　　风从西南方来，名曰谋风。其伤人也，内舍于脾，外在于肌，其气主为弱。风从东南方来，名曰弱风。其伤人也，内舍于胃，外在肌肉，其气主体重。[23p]

    Nine Palaces and Eight Winds

    The wind comes from the southwest, called the "Strategic Wind." Its harm affects the inner spleen and manifests externally on the skin; its nature is weak. The wind comes from the southeast, known as the "Weak Wind." Its harm affects the inner stomach and shows externally on the muscles; its nature is heavy.[23p]

    　　　　　九针篇

    　　形乐志乐，病生于肉，治之以针石。形数惊恐，筋脉不通，病生于不仁，治之以按摩醪药。　　 【注　形乐志乐，则心广体胖，故当治之针石以疏气。惊伤心肝，恐则伤肾，是以形数惊恐，则筋脉不通，荣气不行，则为不仁。】
    　　　　扁鹊难经

    　　　　　肌肉消瘦

    　　三损损于肌肉，肌肉消瘦，饮食不能为肌肤。
    　　　　中藏经 【汉　华佗】

    　　　　　肉痹

    　　肉痹者，饮食不节，膏粱肥美之所为也。痹者肉之奉，气已食痹者肉之本，气已食[　疑作「脾者肉之本，气已失」]。则肉不荣，肌肤不泽则纹理疏。凡风寒暑湿之邪易为入，故不早治则为肉痹。肉痹之状，其先能食而不能充悦，四肢缓而不收持者也。其右关脉按举皆无力而往来濇也。宜节饮食以调其脏，常起居以安其痹，然后依经补泻，以求其愈也。[24p]

    Nine Needle Treatise

    The joy of the body leads to the joy of the heart; illness arises from the flesh, treated with needles and stones. When the body experiences shock and fear, the channels and meridians become blocked. Illness arises from lack of kindness, treated with massage and medicinal potions.

    Notes: The joy of the body and heart means that when the heart is broad and the body is plump, it is necessary to treat with needles and stones to disperse qi. Shock harms the heart and liver, and fear harms the kidneys; hence, when the body experiences shock and fear, the channels and meridians become obstructed, and the nourishing qi does not flow, leading to a lack of kindness.

    Bian Que's Difficult Classics

    Muscle Atrophy

    When there are three losses affecting the muscles, the muscles become thin, and food cannot nourish the skin.

    Central Storage Classics (Han: Hua Tuo)

    Muscle Obstruction

    Muscle obstruction occurs due to irregular eating habits, the consequence of rich and fatty foods. Obstruction refers to the support of the flesh, where qi has already consumed the essence of the flesh, leading to no nourishment for the muscles, and the skin lacks moisture, resulting in loose texture. Environmental factors like wind, cold, heat, and dampness easily invade; thus, if not treated early, it leads to muscle obstruction. The condition of muscle obstruction begins with the inability to feel satisfaction despite eating. The limbs are weak and unable to hold themselves. The right pulse feels weak and lacks rhythm. One should regulate diet to balance the organs, maintain a regular routine to soothe the obstruction, and then follow the classics for supplementation and drainage to seek recovery.[24p]

    　　　　　肉病治疗

    　　按摩则可以驱浮淫于肌肉，宜按摩而不按摩，则使人淫堕肌肉，久留未消。　　病若虚而不补，则使人气血消散，肌肉耗亡，精神脱失，志意昏迷。不当汗而汗，则令人肌肉消绝，津液枯耗。不当按摩而按摩，则使人肌肉(月真)胀，筋骨舒张。
    　　　　千金方 【唐　孙思邈】

    　　　　　肉极

    　　凡肉极者，主脾也。脾应肉，肉与脾合。若脾病则肉变色。又曰：至阴遇病为肌痹，肌痹不已，复感于邪，内舍于脾，体痒淫淫如鼠走，其人身上津液脱，腠理开，汗大泄，鼻端色黄，是其相也。凡风气藏于皮肤，肉色则败。以季夏戊己日伤于风为脾风。脾风之状多汗。阴动伤寒，寒则虚，虚则体重怠惰，四肢不欲举，不嗜饮食，食则咳，咳则右胁下痛引肩背，不可以动转，名曰厉风，里虚外实。[25p]

    Treatment of Flesh Diseases

    Massaging can dispel superficial evils affecting the muscles; it is advisable to massage rather than refrain from doing so, as not massaging will lead to indulgence in the muscle, lingering for a long time without dissipating. If a disease is deficient and not supplemented, it causes the qi and blood to disperse, the muscles to weaken, the spirit to diminish, and the will to become muddled. Sweating inappropriately leads to the extinction of muscles and depletion of bodily fluids. Inappropriate massage can cause muscle swelling and relaxation of tendons and bones.
    — Qianjin Fang [Tang Dynasty, Sun Simiao]

    The Extremes of Flesh

    In general, the extremes of flesh correspond to the spleen. The spleen is associated with flesh, and the flesh harmonizes with the spleen. If the spleen is diseased, the flesh changes color. Moreover, it is said: when the extreme yin encounters illness, it leads to muscular atrophy; if muscular atrophy persists and is further affected by external evils, residing within the spleen, the body itches as if mice are running, and the bodily fluids escape, the pores open, resulting in profuse sweating, with a yellowish hue at the tip of the nose which is its sign. Generally, when wind and qi accumulate in the skin, the color of the flesh deteriorates. The spleen wind occurs in the late summer when the earth element is injured by the wind. The conditions of spleen wind are characterized by excessive sweating. When yin movement is injured by cold, it leads to deficiency; deficiency results in a heavy and lethargic body, with limbs reluctant to move, lacking appetite. If food is consumed, it causes coughing; coughing then results in pain under the right ribs that radiates to the shoulder and back, restricting movement. This condition is called severe wind, with internal deficiency and external fullness.[25p]

    若阳动伤热，热则实，实则人身上如鼠走，唇口坏，皮肤色变，身体津液脱，腠理开，汗大泄，名曰恶风。须决其纲纪，知其终始，阴阳动静，肉之虚实，实则泻之，虚则补之。能治其病者，风始入肉皮毛肌肤筋脉之间，即须决之。若入六腑五脏则半死矣。扁鹊曰：肉绝不治，五日死。何以知之？皮肤不通，外不得泄。凡肉应足太阴，太阴气绝则脉不荣其肌肉。口唇者，肌肉之本也。脉不荣则肌肉濡，肌肉濡则人中满，人中满则唇反，唇反气尽则肉先死。甲笃乙死，木胜土死，良医妙药，终不治也。
    　　　　　虚实[26p]

    If yang moves and injures heat, then heat becomes real; when real, it feels as if mice are running on the body, the lips and mouth decay, the skin color changes, and bodily fluids are lost, leading to open pores and excessive sweating, which is called evil wind. One must determine its regulations, understand its beginnings and ends, and discern the dynamics of yin and yang and the fullness and emptiness of flesh. When it is full, one must drain it; when it is empty, one must replenish it. To treat the illness, if wind has just entered between the flesh, skin, and sinew, it must be dealt with immediately. If it has entered the six bowels and five organs, it is nearly fatal. Bian Que said: “Without decisive action, death will occur in five days.” How do we know this? When the skin does not open, external substances cannot be expelled. Flesh should correspond to the greater yin; if the qi of the greater yin is exhausted, the pulse will not nourish the flesh. The lips are the foundation of the flesh. If the pulse does not nourish, then the flesh weakens; if the flesh weakens, the middle of the mouth fills, and if the mouth fills, the lips will revert. If the lips revert and qi is exhausted, the flesh will perish first. A's death brings about B's demise; wood conquers earth and leads to death; without good doctors and miraculous medicines, one ultimately cannot be cured.
    Emptiness and Fullness.[26p]

    　　夫肉虚者，坐不安席，身危变动；肉实者坐安不动，喘气。肉虚实之应主于脾。若其腑脏有病从肉生，热则应脏，寒则应腑。
    　　　　河间六书 【金　刘完素】

    　　　　　麻木

    　　风寒湿三气，留着不去，即四肢麻木拘挛也。　　濇者，物湿则滑泽，干则濇滞，燥湿相反故也。如遍身中外濇滞，皆属燥金之化，故秋脉濇，然麻亦犹濇山。由水液衰少而燥濇，气行壅滞而不得滑泽通利，气强攻冲而为麻也。如平人抑其手足，则其气顿行之甚，而濇滞壅碍不得通利，而麻亦犹鼓物之象也。其不欲动者，动则为阳，使气行之转甚，故转麻也。俗方治麻病多用乌、附者，令气行之暴甚，以故转麻因之冲开道路，以得通利，药气尽则平，气行通而麻愈也。然六气不必一气独为病，气有相兼。若亡液为燥，或麻而无热证，即当此方。或风热胜湿为燥因而病麻，则宜以追风散热、活血养液、润燥通气之凉药调之，则麻自愈也。治诸燥濇，悉如此法。[27p]

    When the flesh is deficient, one cannot sit still; the body is unstable and restless. When the flesh is strong, one can sit comfortably and breathe easily. The response of the flesh's deficiency or fullness is governed by the spleen. If the organs are sick due to the flesh, heat will affect the organs, while cold will affect the bowels.

    Numbness

    When the three forces of wind, cold, and dampness linger without leaving, the limbs become numb and constricted. Dampness causes smoothness; dryness causes stagnation. Thus, because dryness and dampness oppose each other, if there is stagnation throughout the body, it belongs to the transformation of dry metal, hence numbness in autumn. However, numbness is also similar to stagnation. Due to the scarcity of water and fluids, dryness leads to numbness, and when the flow of qi is obstructed, it does not achieve smoothness and clarity. If vitality is strong but struggles violently, it results in numbness. If a healthy person suppresses their limbs, their qi will suddenly move vigorously, causing stagnation and obstruction, and numbness resembles the effect of a drum on an object. Those who do not wish to move will become numb upon movement since movement increases yang, making qi surge. Thus, numbness arises. Common prescriptions for treating numbness often use black and foxglove herbs to stimulate qi flow vigorously. This creates an opening to achieve smoothness; when the medicinal properties are exhausted, balance is restored, and qi flows freely, leading to recovery from numbness. However, the six qi do not necessarily act singularly to cause illness; they often coexist. If fluids are lost leading to dryness, or there is numbness without heat symptoms, this treatment should be considered. If wind and heat overpower dampness causing dryness and resulting in numbness, one should use herbs that expel wind, dispel heat, invigorate blood, nourish fluids, and moisten dryness to regulate and thereby resolve numbness. The treatment for all kinds of dryness and stagnation should follow this principle.[27p]

    　　　　明理论 【金　成无己】

    　　　　　不仁

    　　伤寒肉不仁，何以明之？仁，柔也。不仁，不柔和也，痒不知也，痛不知也，寒不知也，热不知也。任其屈伸，灸刺不知，所以然者是谓不仁也。由邪气壅盛，正气为邪气闭伏，郁而不发，荣卫血气虚少，不能通行致斯然也。《内经》曰：荣气虚则不仁。《针经》曰：卫气不行则为不仁。经曰：荣卫不能相将，三焦无所仰，身体痹不仁。即是言之，知荣卫血气虚少，不能通行为不仁者明矣。经曰：诸乘寒者，则为厥郁冒不仁。[28p]

    Theory of Clarity
    (Jin Cheng Wu Ji)

    Unkindness

    In the case of cold-induced numbness of the flesh, how can one clarify it? Kindness is softness. Unkindness is not softness; it is the inability to feel itching, pain, cold, or heat. When one allows the body to bend and stretch without awareness of these sensations, one is said to be unkind. This arises due to the excessive obstruction of pathogenic qi, causing the rightful qi to be suppressed and unable to emerge, leading to the deficiency of nutrative and defensive blood qi, thus failing to circulate properly. The "Inner Canon" states that when the nutrative qi is deficient, one experiences unkindness. The "Needle Classic" states that when the defensive qi does not circulate, it leads to unkindness. The classics say: when the nutrative and defensive forces cannot support each other, the triple burner has no elevation, and the body experiences numbness and unkindness. Therefore, it is made clear that understanding the deficiency of the nutrative and defensive blood qi, which cannot flow properly, results in unkindness. The classics state: those who succumb to the cold will suffer from obstruction and thus experience unkindness.[28p]

    言此厥者，是正气为寒气所乘为厥气也，非四肢逆冷之厥也。何者？盖以郁冒为昏冒，不仁为不知痛痒，得不为尸厥之厥耶？经曰：少阴脉不至，肾气微，少精血，奔气促迫，上入胸膈，宗气反聚，血结心下，阳气退下，热归阴股，与阴相动，令身不仁，此为尸厥。其乘寒之厥，郁冒不仁，即此尸厥可知矣。昔越人入虢，诊太子为尸厥，以郁冒不仁为可治，刺之而得痊愈者，实神医之诊也。鸣呼！设或脉浮而洪，身汗如油，喘而不休，水浆不下，形体不仁，此谓命绝，虽越人其能起之欤？[29p]

    This text refers to the condition known as "sudden loss of consciousness" caused by the invasion of cold from the environment into the body, rather than from the extremities being cold. Why is this? It is because stagnation leading to dizziness and insensitivity results in an inability to feel pain or discomfort, which can indeed be classified as a type of "sudden loss of consciousness." The classic text states: when the lesser yin pulse is absent, the kidney's vitality is weak, there is a lack of essence and blood, and the rushing qi is forced upwards into the chest cavity, the ancestral qi gathers back, causing blood to stagnate beneath the heart, the yang qi retreats, heat returns to the yin, creating a mutual movement that renders the body insensitive, this is called "sudden loss of consciousness." The symptoms caused by cold invasion, along with stagnation and insensitivity, clearly indicate this type of "sudden loss of consciousness." In ancient times, when the people of Yue entered Guo, they diagnosed the prince's condition as "sudden loss of consciousness" based on stagnation and insensitivity, believing it to be treatable, and they performed acupuncture, resulting in a cure; this truly reflects the skill of a divine healer. Oh! If someone has a pulse that is floating and surging, sweats profusely, experiences continuous shortness of breath, cannot take in liquids, and their body is insensitive, this is called life-threatening, and even the people of Yue would find it difficult to revive such a person.[29p]

    　　　　　瞤动

    　　经曰：动气在左，不可发汗，发汗则头眩，汗不止，筋惕肉瞤。是发汗而动肝气者也。　　伤寒肉瞤，何以明之？伤寒头痛身疼，恶寒发热者，必然之证也。其于肉瞤，非常常有之者，必待发汗过多，亡阳则有之矣。《内经》曰：阳气者，精则养神，柔则养筋。发汗过多，津液枯少，阳气太虚，筋肉失所养，故惕惕然而跳，瞤瞤然而动也。太阳病脉微弱，汗出恶风者，不可服大青龙汤，服之则厥逆，筋惕肉瞤，此为逆也。[30p]

    Trembling

    The classics say: When the qi moves to the left, sweating should not be induced; if sweating occurs, it leads to dizziness and if the sweat does not stop, the muscles and flesh tremble. This occurs when sweating stimulates the liver qi. How can we clarify the muscle trembling in the case of cold damage? Cold damage typically presents with headaches, body aches, aversion to cold, and fever—these are inevitable signs. The muscle trembling is usually caused by excessive sweating; when yang is lost, it manifests. The "Inner Canon" states: Yang qi nourishes the spirit when it is refined and nourishes the muscles when it is gentle. Excessive sweating leads to depletion of fluids and weakened yang qi, causing the muscles to lose their nourishment, which results in trembling and involuntary movements. In cases of taiyang disease where the pulse is weak and sweating occurs with aversion to wind, one should not take the major green dragon decoction; taking it would lead to counterflow and muscular trembling, marking a reversal.[30p]

    太阳病发汗，汗出不解，其人仍发热，头眩身瞤动，振振欲擗地者，真武汤主之。动气在左，不可发汗，发汗则头眩，汗不止，筋惕肉瞤。即是观之，筋惕肉瞤，由发汗多亡阳，则阳虚可见矣。兹虽逆也，止于发汗亡阳而表虚，治以温经益阳则可矣。或因吐下发汗，表里俱虚而有此状者，又非若但发汗后所可同也。经曰：伤寒吐下发汗，虚烦，脉甚微，八九日心下痞鞕，胁下痛，气上冲咽喉，眩冒筋脉动惕者，久而成痿。此为逆之甚者也。太阳病发汗复下之后，表里俱虚，复加烧针，因胸烦面色青黄肤瞤者难治。兹为逆之甚者也。发汗吐下，庸可忽诸！
    　　　　儒门事亲 【元　张从政】

    　　　　　不仁

    　　凡肌肉不仁，乃风湿寒三气合而为痹，及手足麻痹不仁。《内经》曰：荣虚卫实，皮肤不仁，痹而不知痒痛，可用郁金散吐之，次服导水丸轻寒之药泄之；泄讫，次以辛温之剂。汗出后，常服当归、芍药、乌、附行经和血之药，则愈矣。[31p]

    In cases of Taiyang disease, if sweating is induced and the sweat does not resolve the fever, but the person continues to have fever, with dizziness and body trembling, and a sensation of wanting to hit the ground, this is treated with Zhenwu Decoction. If the movement of qi is on the left, sweating should not be induced; if it is induced, it will lead to dizziness, unceasing sweat, and trembling of the tendons and flesh. This indicates that the excessive sweating has consumed Yang, revealing Yang deficiency. Though this may seem contrary, it is necessary to stop the sweating that depletes Yang and leads to exterior deficiency, and treat with warming the meridians and nourishing Yang. If someone has symptoms of deficiency at both the exterior and interior due to vomiting, purging, and sweating, this is not the same as just the aftermath of sweating alone. The classics say: in cases of cold damage with vomiting, purging, and sweating, if there is vexation and the pulse is very weak, after eight or nine days there may be distention below the heart, pain in the sides, qi surging to the throat, dizziness, and movement of the tendons, which can lead to atrophy over time. This indicates a severe reversal. After sweating, vomiting, and purging in a case of Taiyang disease, if both the exterior and interior are deficient, and there are additional symptoms like chest distress, and a blue-yellow complexion with trembling skin, treatment is difficult. This is the gravest reversal. Sweating, vomiting, and purging should not be neglected!

    Regarding the matter of unfeelingness:

    If the flesh is unfeeling, it is due to a combination of wind, dampness, and cold leading to obstruction, along with numbness in the hands and feet. The Neijing states: with deficient nourishment and replete defenses, the skin is unfeeling and cannot sense itch or pain. One may use Yujin Powder for vomiting, and then take Daoshui Pill and lighter cold medications to purge; once purged, follow with spicy warming agents. After sweating, regularly taking medicines such as angelica, peony, rehmannia, and prepared aconite to harmonize the blood will lead to recovery.[31p]

    　　　　东垣十书 【元　李杲】

    　　　　　痿痛消削

    　　脾气热，生肉痿，故痹而不仁。诸痿皆属于上者，指病之本在肺也，故必先于起肺，然后热传入五脏，散为诸证。　　肌肉痿，足太阳膀胱经也。
    　　肉痛，足太阴脾经也。
    　　脾虚则肌肉消削，盖人之肉如地之土，岂可人而无肉？故肉消则死矣。
    　　　　丹溪心法 【元　朱震亨】

    　　　　　麻木

    　　麻是气虚，木是湿痰死血。或有气血俱虚，但麻而不木者；有虚而感湿，麻木兼作者；有因虚而风寒湿三气乘之，故周身掣痛麻木并作者。若此其甚，宜先汗而后补。有痰滞四肢，或一指麻木，逾年而有中风之病，此皆气血先虚之兆也。若此者，须预治之。[32p]

    Eastern Garden Ten Treatises
    (Yuan - Li Gao)

    Debility and Pain Reduction

    The heat of the spleen causes muscular debility, leading to numbness and loss of feeling. All forms of debility are linked to the upper regions; the root of the illness is in the lungs. Therefore, one must first address the lungs, after which the heat can move into the five organs, dispersing into various symptoms.
    Muscular debility is associated with the Foot Taiyang Bladder Meridian.
    Pain in the flesh is related to the Foot Taiyin Spleen Meridian.
    When the spleen is weak, the muscles diminish, as a person's flesh is like the soil of the earth; how could a person exist without flesh? Therefore, if the flesh diminishes, death will follow.

    Danxi Heart Method
    (Yuan - Zhu Zhenheng)

    Numbness

    Numbness is associated with qi deficiency; "wood" refers to phlegm and stagnant blood. There may be cases of both qi and blood deficiency, resulting in numbness without the presence of phlegm. If there is deficiency accompanied by dampness, one experiences numbness alongside other symptoms. In cases where deficiency is compounded by the three factors of wind, cold, and damp, the whole body may experience pulling pain and numbness. In severe cases, one should expel the excess through sweating before supplementing. If phlegm stagnates in the limbs or if just one finger becomes numb for over a year, it may indicate a risk of stroke; these are all signs of prior qi and blood deficiency. Such conditions must be treated in advance.[32p]

    　　　　医学正传 【明　虞抟】

    　　　　　麻木

    　　经曰：风寒湿三气，合而为痹，故风气胜者为行痹，寒气胜者为痛痹，湿气胜者为着痹。河间曰：留着不去，四肢麻木拘挛也。又曰：痛者，寒气多也，有寒故痛。其不痛不仁者，病久入深，荣卫之行濇，经络时疏，故不痛；皮肤不荣，故为不仁。夫所谓不仁者，或周身，或四肢唧唧然麻木不知痛痒，如绳扎缚初解之状，古方名为麻痹者是也。丹溪曰：麻是气虚，木是湿痰死血。然则曰麻曰木者，以不仁中分而为二也。虽然，亦有气血俱虚，但麻而不木者；亦有虚而感湿，麻木兼作者；又有因虚而风寒湿三气乘之，故周身掣痛，兼麻木并作者，古方谓之周痹。治法宜先汗而后补也。医者宜各以类推而治之，不可执一见也。[33p]

    Medical Transmission - Ming Dynasty, Yu Tuan

    Numbness

    The classics say: The three energies of wind, cold, and dampness combine to create blockages. Hence, when wind prevails, it causes moving blockages; when cold prevails, it causes painful blockages; and when dampness prevails, it causes stagnation. He Jian states: If it lingers and does not go away, the limbs become numb and constrained. It further states: When there is pain, it is due to excessive cold; pain arises from cold. When there is no pain or numbness, it indicates a prolonged illness that has penetrated deeply. The flow of nourishment is sluggish, and the meridians are sometimes obstructed, thus there is no pain; the skin is not nourished, resulting in numbness. The so-called numbness can affect the entire body or just the limbs, leading to a tingling, numbing sensation without awareness of pain or itch, similar to the state after a rope has been released from tight binding. The ancient texts referred to this as numbness. Danxi mentions: Numbness relates to Qi deficiency, while 'wood' symbolizes dampness, phlegm, and stagnant blood. Therefore, referring to numbness and 'wood' is a way of distinguishing two kinds of numbness. Nonetheless, there can be cases of both Qi and blood deficiency that present only numbness without 'wood'; there are also cases where deficiency causes dampness, leading to both numbness and pain; further, there can be conditions where deficiency allows the three energies of wind, cold, and dampness to invade, resulting in pain and numbness throughout the body. Ancient texts termed this as generalized blockage. The treatment method should prioritize sweating first, followed by supplementation. Physicians should apply similar principles to treat, rather than adhering to a single viewpoint.[33p]

    　　　　　脉法

    　　脉浮而濡，属气虚。关前得之，麻在上体；关后得之，麻在下体也。　　脉浮而缓，属湿，为麻痹；脉紧而浮，属寒，为痛痹；脉濇而芤，属死血，为木，不知痛痒。
    　　　　医学纲目 【明　楼英】

    　　　　　肉部所主

    　　脾主肉。经云：脾主肉。在体为肉，在脏为脾。又云：邪在脾胃，则病肌肉痛是也。　　脾病在溪。经云：北方黑色，入通于肾，故病在溪。溪者，肉之小会也。
    　　　　　病因
    　　湿伤肉，甘伤肉。经云，湿伤肉，风胜湿。甘伤肉，酸胜甘。又云，甘走肉，肉病无多食甘。又云，多食酸则肉胝(月刍)而唇揭是也。　　坐乐伤肉。经云：久坐伤肉。又云：形乐志乐，病生于肉，治之以针石是也。
    　　　　医宗必读 【明　李中梓】[34p]

    Pulse Diagnosis

    A floating and moist pulse indicates Qi deficiency. If it is felt in the front gate, the condition affects the upper body; if felt in the back gate, it affects the lower body. A floating and relaxed pulse indicates dampness, leading to paralysis; a tight and floating pulse indicates cold, leading to painful obstruction; a choppy and hollow pulse indicates stagnant blood, belonging to Wood, with no sensation of pain or itch.

    Muscle Functions

    The spleen governs muscle. The classic states: the spleen governs muscle; in the body it is the muscle, in the organs it is the spleen. Moreover, if there is evil in the spleen and stomach, muscle pain will result. Spleen illness is located in the creek. The classic states: in the northern direction, black corresponds with the kidneys, hence illness in the creek. The creek is the minor convergence of muscle.

    Causes of Illness

    Dampness injures the muscles, sweetness harms the muscles. The classic states: dampness injures the muscles, wind overcomes dampness. Sweetness harms the muscles, sourness overcomes sweetness. Furthermore, excessive sweetness leads to muscle diseases; consuming a lot of sourness causes muscular stiffness and lip peeling. Prolonged sitting injures the muscles. The classic states: prolonged sitting damages muscles. Moreover, emotional joy and physical delight can lead to ailments in the muscles, which should be treated with needles and stones.[34p]

    　　　　　肉脱者死

    　　形肉已脱，九候虽调犹此，此岐伯欲人以脉合形也。盖形肉者脾之所主，脾土为万物之母，观其形肉脱则知脾坏于内而根本丧矣。九候虽调，犹不免于死，形可以弗视乎哉！
    　　　　　肉痿

    　　经云：脾气热则胃干而渴，肌肉不仁，发为肉痿。盖脾痿者，肉痿也。脾与胃以膜相连，而开窍于口，故脾热则胃干而渴。脾主肌肉，热蓄于内则精气耗伤，故肌肉不仁，发为肉痿。
    　　　　古今医鉴 【明　龚信】

    　　　　　脾痹

    　　痹病在肌者多不仁，应乎脾，其证四肢懈怠，发嗽呕吐。
    　　　　　麻木

    　　肌肉麻木者，因风湿热下陷入血分阴中，阳道不利，亦有痰在血分者。其证合眼则浑身肌肉麻木痒者，血不荣于肌腠，治以参、芪能助阳道，以当归能行阴道，二朮、苓、甘、蘗以除湿热，柴、升、芍药以升提之。痰加二陈。治当活法。　　如感风湿，手膊或痛或木，或遍身肌肉麻木，用五积散主之。[35p]

    Death from Flesh Loss

    When the flesh has fully detached, despite the nine conditions being regulated, it is still like this. Qi Bo desires that one understands the pulse aligned with the form. The flesh is governed by the spleen, which is the source of all things. Observing the flesh's detachment indicates internal damage to the spleen, leading to a loss of foundation. Even if the nine conditions are adjusted, one cannot escape death; how can the form be overlooked?

    Muscle Atrophy

    The scripture states: When spleen qi is hot, the stomach dries and thirst arises, causing the muscles to become numb, leading to muscle atrophy. The atrophy of the spleen results in muscle atrophy. The spleen and stomach are interconnected by membranes, opening at the mouth. Therefore, if spleen heat occurs, the stomach dries and causes thirst. The spleen governs muscles; internal heat depletes vital essence, resulting in numb muscles, leading to muscle atrophy.

    Spleen Obstruction

    Obstruction diseases affecting the muscles often lead to numbness, corresponding to the spleen. The symptoms include weakness in the limbs, coughing, and vomiting.

    Numbness

    Muscle numbness occurs due to wind, dampness, and heat descending into the blood division's yin. The yang pathway is obstructed, and there may also be phlegm in the blood division. Symptoms include general muscle numbness and itching when closing one's eyes, as blood fails to nourish the skin and muscles. Treatments with ginseng and astragalus can help the yang pathway, while angelica can promote the yin pathway. The herbs Atractylodes, Poria, licorice, and rhubarb can eliminate damp heat, and schisandra, perilla, and peony can uplift the condition. Phlegm requires treatment with Er Chen. Treatment should be effective; if encountering wind and dampness, the arms may feel painful or numb, or the entire body may experience muscle numbness. Use Wu Ji San for this.[35p]

    　　　　医学准绳六要 【明　张三锡】
    　　　　　脾应肉

    　　五脏一或有虚，必见证于外，脾虚则面与手足肌肉削肿，因其流而补其源，可谓上工矣。
    　　　　　痿瘦

    　　心脾损及胃损，饮食不为肌肤，宜益气和血调饮食，十全大补汤、补肾金刚丸。
    　　　　　肉极

    　　脾实则肌肉痹，腠理开，汗大泄，四肢缓弱急痛，宜薏苡仁散。
    　　　　　麻木

    　　荣卫滞而不行则麻木，如久坐压住一处，麻不能举，理可见矣。麻属痰属虚，木则全属湿痰死血，一块不知痛痒，若木然是也。　　脉沉滑体厚人，多痰与湿，二朮二陈，或少佐风药羌、独、桂枝一二味，兼参、芪补气。　　妇人及素有郁抑者，当舒郁。[36p]

    Principles of Medicine: Six Essentials
    (Ming Dynasty, Zhang Sanxi)

    Spleen Corresponds to Flesh
    If there is deficiency in any of the five organs, it will manifest externally. When the spleen is deficient, the face and limbs will exhibit weak and swollen muscles. One should channel the flow and replenish the source, which can be considered a skillful approach.

    Emaciation
    When the heart and spleen are compromised, leading to stomach damage, food does not nourish the skin and flesh. It is advisable to tonify qi and harmonize blood with appropriate diet, remedies like the Ten Benefits Great Tonifying Decoction, and Kidney-strengthening Pills.

    Extreme Flesh
    When the spleen is full, it leads to muscular obstruction, the pores open, resulting in profuse sweating and weak limbs with urgent pain. One should take Job’s Tears Powder.

    Numbness
    When the nutrients and defenses stagnate and do not circulate, numbness occurs, similar to prolonged pressure on one area, causing inability to lift—this can be understood. Numbness is related to phlegm and deficiency; wood corresponds entirely to damp phlegm and stagnant blood, which causes insensitivity to pain or itch, leading to a state of numbness. Those with a deep, slippery pulse and a robust body are often afflicted with phlegm and dampness. Using the combinations of the two herbs of Atractylodes and Pinellia, along with possibly a few additional herbs for wind like Qiang, Duan, and Cinnamon Twig, while also incorporating Ginseng and Astragalus for qi replenishment, is beneficial.
    For women and those with a history of repression, it is essential to clear the stagnation.[36p]

    　　脉微弱或弦大无力，病久体羸者，血气虚，补中益气。或加制附子一片，夏月对生脉散。　　一块不知痛痒，阴寒益甚，或日轻夜重，脉濇而芤。　　痰挟死血，宜活血行气，芎、归、桃仁泥、红花、牛膝、二陈之类加韭汁。大便黑而闭者，桃仁承气汤下之。
    　　　　伤寒六书 【明　陶华】

    　　　　　瞤惕

    　　肉瞤筋惕者，非常常有之。阳气者，精则养神，柔则养筋。发汗过多，津液涸少，阳气偏枯，筋肉失所养，故惕惕然动，瞤瞤然跳也。非温经助阳之药，何可愈乎？故设真武汤以救之。因汗吐下后，表里俱虚，有此证者，逆之甚也。
    　　　　　不仁

    　　肌肉不仁者，谓不柔和，虽痛痒不知，针火不知是也。诸虚乘寒，则为郁冒不仁，血气虚弱，不能周流于一身，于是正气为邪气所伏，故肢体顽麻不仁，厥如死尸，用桂麻各半汤。不愈者，补中益气汤，入姜汁。设或身体如油，汗出不休，喘而直视，水浆不入者，此为命绝也。[37p]

    The pulse is weak or feels large and powerless; for those who have been ill for a long time and are emaciated, the blood and qi are deficient, so one should tonify the middle and benefit the qi. Alternatively, add a piece of processed aconite and use Sheng Mai San in summer.

    If one feels no pain or discomfort but experiences increased coldness, with symptoms that are lighter during the day and heavier at night, the pulse will be weak and hollow.

    Phlegm mixed with stagnant blood should be treated with blood-activating and qi-moving herbs, such as Chuanxiong, Angelica, peach kernel mud, safflower, Notopterygium, and the two Chen herbs, combined with chives. For dark stools and constipation, use Peach Kernel Chengqi Decoction to relieve it.

    In cases of cold damage, one may experience tremors, which are not uncommon. Yang qi, when adequate, nourishes the spirit and when gentle, nourishes the tendons. Excessive sweating leads to depletion of fluids, and when yang qi is deficient, the muscles and tendons lose nourishment, causing tremors and spasms. Without warming the channels and assisting yang with medicine, how can one expect improvement? Therefore, Shen Wu Decoction is prescribed to rescue this condition. After sweating, vomiting, or purging, when both exterior and interior are deficient, these symptoms are especially serious.

    Numbness of the muscles refers to a lack of softness and sensitivity; even with pain or itching, one remains unaware, unable to feel needles or fire applied to the skin. When various deficiencies coincide with cold, this results in malaise and numbness. If blood and qi are weak and cannot circulate throughout the body, upright qi is suppressed by evil qi, which leads to limbs being stubbornly numb and lifeless as if they were dead. Use a decoction of equal parts cinnamon and麻 also. If this does not resolve the issue, then use the Zhongyi Yiqi Decoction with ginger juice.

    If the body feels oily, sweating does not cease, breathing is labored, and one cannot take in water, this indicates a critical condition.[37p]

    　　　　古今医统 【明　徐春甫】

    　　　　　麻木论

    　　《内经》以风寒湿三气杂至，合而为痹，其风气胜者为行痹，寒气胜者为痛痹，湿气胜者为着痹。其不痛不仁者为麻痹是也。今夫麻木之证，正经所谓不痛不仁。病久入深，荣卫之行濇，经络时疏，故不痛，皮肤不荣，故不仁，如绳扎缚初解之状。
    　　　　　治麻木以疏导郁滞为先

    　　凡坐卧及倚靠之久，而致经络气血不通，即麻而木，可见其郁滞也。凡麻木多在四肢及手足之指者，此则四末气血不充，荣不通，故多麻木也。丹溪谓当多用附子行经，则此意也。　　十指麻木者，胃中多有湿痰死血，宜二陈汤加苍白朮、桃仁、红花之类。
    　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

    　　　　　麻木[38p]

    The Treatise on Numbness

    In the "Neijing," it states that the combination of the three Qi: wind, cold, and dampness results in bi syndrome. When wind predominates, it is termed "xingshi," when cold predominates, it is "tongbi," and when dampness predominates, it is "zhangbi." The state of being neither painful nor sensitive is called numbness. Currently, the symptom of numbness aligns with the classic definition of being neither painful nor sensitive. When an illness has persisted for a long time, it penetrates deeply, causing the flow of nourishment and defense to become sluggish, leading to the obstruction of meridians, hence the absence of pain; the skin lacks nourishment, resulting in insensitivity, much like the condition of a rope that has been tied and then partially loosened.

    To treat numbness, the first step is to disperse and guide the Qi and blood that are stagnant.

    If one sits or lies in a position for an extended time, causing the Qi and blood in the meridians to become unimpeded, numbness will result, indicating stagnation. Numbness predominantly occurs in the limbs and the fingers, suggesting inadequate Qi and blood supply to the extremities, resulting in numbness. Danxi asserts the frequent use of aconite to move the meridians, which aligns with this idea.

    For numbness in all ten fingers, this indicates a significant presence of damp phlegm and stagnant blood in the stomach, for which the prescription of Er Chen Decoction with the addition of Atractylodes Macrocephala, Peach Kernel, and Red Flower is recommended.[38p]

    　　《原病式》列麻证在六气燥金诸濇条下。释之曰：物得湿则滑泽，干则濇滞，麻犹濇也。由水液衰少而燥濇，气行壅滞而不得滑泽通利，气强攻冲而为麻也。俗方治麻病，多用乌、附者，令气行之暴甚，以故转麻，因之冲开道路，以得通利而麻愈也。然六气不必一气独为病，气有相兼。若亡液为燥，或麻木无热证，即当此治。或风热胜湿为燥，因而病麻，则宜以退风散热、活血养液、润燥通气之凉药调之。东垣则曰：麻者，气之虚也，真气弱不能流通，填塞经络，四肢俱虚，故生麻木不仁。或在手，或在足，或通身皮肤尽麻者，皆以黄芪、人参、白朮、甘草、五味、芍药、当归、升麻、柴胡之类，随时令所乘之气，出入无方，但补其虚，全不用攻冲之峻剂。窃详刘、李二公，生同时，居同地，无世运方土之异宜，何乃凡病遽有补攻之别如此？盖因悟入圣人之道不同。刘以人禀天赋，本无亏欠，因邪入搅乱其气，而后成病，所以攻邪为要，邪退则正气自安。[39p]

    The "Original Disease Theory" lists the symptoms of numbness under the categories of the Six Qis, including Dryness and Metal. It explains that when substances gain moisture, they become smooth and moist; when they are dry, they become stagnant. Numbness is akin to stagnation. This results from a deficiency of bodily fluids leading to dryness, and from the obstruction of Qi, which prevents smooth circulation. If Qi becomes strong and forceful, it can create numbness.

    Common remedies for numbness often include the use of black and aconite herbs, which stimulate Qi excessively, thus helping to resolve the stagnation and restore smooth circulation, resulting in the alleviation of numbness. However, the Six Qis do not necessarily imply that any single Qi alone causes disease; multiple Qis can interact. If bodily fluids are lost, leading to dryness, or if there is numbness without heat symptoms, then this must be treated accordingly. If wind-heat overwhelms dampness and leads to numbness, one should use cooling herbs to dispel wind, scatter heat, invigorate blood, nourish fluids, and moisten dryness to facilitate circulation.

    Dongyuan states that numbness signifies a deficiency of Qi. When the vital energy is weak and cannot flow properly, it blocks the meridians, resulting in weakness in the limbs and subsequent numbness. This numbness may occur in the hands or feet, or it may affect the skin overall. Remedies should include Astragalus, Ginseng, Atractylodes, Licorice, Schisandra, Peony, Angelica, Cimicifuga, and Bupleurum, tailored according to the seasonal Qi without rigid prescription, focusing solely on tonifying the deficiency without harshly attacking or forcing the Qi.

    I have noted that both Liu and Li lived in the same era and place, without differences in worldly conditions or geographical suitability. Why then is there such a distinction between their approaches to treatment? This is due to their different understandings of the Way of the Sages. Liu believed that a person is born with innate gifts, and when disturbances from pathogens enter and disrupt the Qi, illness results. Therefore, attacking the pathogen is essential; once the pathogen is expelled, the vital energy can restore its balance.[39p]

    李以人之真气，荣养百骸，周于性命，凡真气失调，少有所亏，则五邪六淫，便得乘间而入，所以补正为要，正复则邪气自却。今宜酌量二公之法，当攻当补，从中调治，无执泥其说。丹溪又分麻木为二，以麻止习习然，尚无气血攻冲不行之状；木则气血已痹不仁，莫知其痛痒也。疠风初起者，其手足必先木而后皮肤疡溃，与夫痈痪者，手足亦时麻木，当自求之本门。　　《素问》曰：荣气虚则不仁，卫气虚则不用，荣卫俱虚则不仁且不用。《灵枢》曰：卫气不行，则必麻木。[40p]

    Using the true qi of a person nourishes the hundred bones and circulates throughout life. Whenever the true qi is out of balance and suffers even a little, the five evils and six afflictions can take the opportunity to invade. Therefore, the key is to supplement and correct; when the correct qi is restored, the evil qi will naturally retreat. Now, it is advisable to carefully consider the methods of the two gentlemen, to know when to attack and when to supplement, and adjust accordingly without being rigid in their theories. Danxi further divides numbness into two types; one type called "ma" merely stops habits and still shows no signs of the disturbance of qi and blood, while "wood" indicates that qi and blood have been obstructed and are unresponsive, lacking awareness of pain and itching. When an epidemic wind first arises, the hands and feet will certainly first show signs of "wood" and then the skin will ulcerate; similarly, in cases of boils and paralysis, the hands and feet can also become numb. One should seek the origins of this. The "Suwen" states: when the nourishing qi is weak, there is no responsiveness; when the defensive qi is weak, there is no function; when both the nourishing and defensive qi are weak, there is neither responsiveness nor function. The "Ling Shu" states: if the defensive qi does not flow, then one is bound to experience numbness.[40p]

    东垣治麻痹必补卫气而行之，盖本诸此。　　浑身麻木不仁，或左、或右半身麻木，或面、或头、或手臂、或脚腿麻木不仁，并神效黄芪汤。　　皮肤间有麻木，此肺气不行也，芍药补气汤。如肌肉麻必待泻荣而愈。如湿热相合，四肢沉痛，当泻湿热。　　《金匮》方血痹阴阳俱微，寸口关上微，尺中小紧，外证身体不仁如风痹状，黄芪桂枝五物汤主之。　　湿气风证不退，眩运，麻木不已，除风湿羌活汤主之。　　荣虚卫穴，肌肉不仁，致令(疒帬)重，名曰肉苛，宜前胡散、苦参丸。[41p]

    In Dongyuan's treatment of paralysis, it is essential to supplement the defensive Qi and proceed accordingly; this serves as the fundamental approach.

    For generalized numbness and loss of sensation, whether on the left or right side of the body, or affecting the face, head, arms, or legs, the Huangqi Decoction is effective.

    If the skin feels numb, it indicates that the lung Qi is not circulating; thus, the Shaoyao Qi Decoction should be used. If the muscles are numb, one must clear the nutrients to recover. If damp heat is present, causing heaviness and pain in the limbs, one should expel the dampness and heat.

    According to the "Jinkui," if blood deficiency presents with both Yin and Yang being weak, the pulse at the cun position is faint, and the pulse at the chi position is mildly tight, while external signs show numbness resembling wind blockage, the Huangqi and Guizhi Five Ingredients Decoction should be prescribed.

    If damp wind symptoms persist with dizziness and ongoing numbness, the Qianghuo Decoction for expelling wind and dampness should be used.

    For deficiency of nourishment and protective Qi resulting in muscle numbness leading to heaviness, termed "meat hardness," the Qianhu Powder or Ku Shen Pills are recommended.[41p]

    古今图书集成医部全录卷二百十三

    肉门

    　　　　方

    　　肉极方 【《千金方》，下同】 　治肉热极，肌痹浮淫如鼠走身上，津液脱，腠理开，汗大泄，为脾风，风气藏于皮肤，肉色败，鼻见黄色。　　麻黄　防己一作防风　枳实　细辛　白朮各三两　生姜　附子各四两　甘草　桂心各二两　石膏八两　　右十味，(口父)咀，以水九升，煮麻黄，去沫，下诸药，煮取三升，分三服。[42p]

    Collection of Classical and Modern Books, Medical Section, Volume 213

    Meat Door

    Formula

    Extreme Meat Formula (also referred to in the “Thousand Gold Formula”): For treating extreme meat heat, where the muscles become stiff and there is a sensation of mice running on the body, with fluids depleted and pores opened, leading to profuse sweating, it is due to spleen wind, with wind energy stored in the skin, causing the meat color to decay and the nose to appear yellow.

    Ingredients:

    • Ephedra (Mahuang)
    • Prepared Sicyo (Fangji, also referred to as Fangfeng)
    • Bitter Orange (Zhishi)
    • Asarum (Xixin)
    • Atractylodes (Baizhu) - each 3 taels
    • Fresh Ginger (Shengjiang)
    • Aconite (Fuzhi) - each 4 taels
    • Licorice (Gancao)
    • Cinnamon Twig (Guixin) - each 2 taels
    • Gypsum (Shigao) - 8 taels

    Combine the ten ingredients, grind them, and boil with 9 sheng of water. Remove the foam, add the remaining medicinal herbs, and boil down to 3 sheng. Divide into three doses.[42p]

    　　西州续命汤　治肉极虚热，肌肤淫淫如鼠走身上，津液开泄，或痹不仁，四肢急痛。　　麻黄　生姜各三两　当归　石膏各二两　杏仁四十枚　芎藭　桂心　甘草　黄芩　防风　芍药各一两　　右十一味，(口父)咀，以水九升，先煮麻黄，除沫，下诸药，煮取三升，去滓，分四服，日再。
    　　石楠散　治肉极热，则体上如鼠走，或如风痹，唇口坏，皮肤色变。主诸风大病。　　石楠三十铢　薯蓣　白芍药一作甘草　天雄　桃花一作桃仁　甘菊花各一两　黄芪十八铢　山茱萸一两十八铢　真珠十八铢　石膏二两　升麻　葳蕤各一两半　　右十二味，治下筛，酒下方寸匕，日再，食后服。[43p]

    Xi Prefecture Renewing Life Decoction: This treats extreme meat heat, where the skin feels as if mice are running over it, with fluid leakage, potential numbness, and acute pain in the limbs. Ingredients: Ephedra, fresh ginger both three taels; Angelica, gypsum both two taels; forty apricot kernels; ligusticum, cinnamon bark, licorice, scutellaria, siler, and peony each one tael. Combine the eleven ingredients, macerate, and with nine quarts of water, first boil the ephedra, remove the scum, add the other herbs, boil until reduced to three quarts, strain, and divide into four doses to be taken twice daily.

    Stone Grape Powder: This treats extreme heat in the flesh, resulting in sensations of mice running on the body, possible wind blockages, broken lips, and discoloration of the skin. It is primarily for severe wind conditions. Ingredients: Thirty grains of stone grape; dioscorea, white peony (or licorice), celestial warrior, peach flower (or peach kernel), and chrysanthemum flower each one tael; eighteen grains of astragalus; one tael and eighteen grains of cornel fruit; eighteen grains of genuine pearl; two taels of gypsum; and half a tael each of stem motherwort and ephedra. Combine the twelve ingredients, crush, and take with alcohol using a half-inch spoon, twice daily after meals.[43p]

    　　大黄芪酒　治肉极虚寒为脾风，阴动伤寒，体重怠惰，四肢不欲举，关节疼痛，不嗜饮食，虚极所致。　　黄芪　桂心　巴戟天　石斛　柏子仁　泽泻　茯苓　干姜　蜀椒各三两　防风　独活　人参各二两　天雄　芍药　附子　乌头　茵芋　半夏　细辛　花粉　白朮　黄芩　山萸各一两　　右二十三味，(口父)咀，绢袋贮，以清酒三斗渍之，秋冬七日，春夏三日，初服三合，渐渐加，微痹为度，日再。　　又方　治肉极虚寒，卒中风，口噤不能言，四肢缓纵，偏挛急痛，注五脏，恍惚，喜怒无常，手脚不随。　　独活　茵芋　黄芩各三两　甘草　防风　芍药　芎藭　麻黄　葛根各二两　人参一两　乌头三枚　　右十一味，(口父)咀，以水一斗，入竹沥四升合煮，取四升，分四服，日三夜一。[44p]

    Great Huangqi Wine: It treats extreme weakness and cold of the flesh resulting from spleen wind, Yin movement causing cold damage, feelings of heaviness and lethargy, disinclination to lift the limbs, joint pain, lack of appetite, all due to extreme deficiency.

    Ingredients: Huangqi, Guixin, Bajitian, Shihu, Baiziren, Zexie, Fuling, Ganjiang, Shujiao, each three taels; Fangfeng, Duhuo, Renjing, each two taels; Tianxiong, Shaoyao, Fuzi, Wutuo, Yinyi, Banxia, Xixin, Huafen, Baizhu, Huangqin, Shanyu, each one tael.

    These twenty-three ingredients should be chewed and stored in a silk bag, then soaked in three dou of clear wine, for seven days in autumn and winter, and three days in spring and summer. Initially take three he, gradually increase it, just until a mild numbness is felt, twice a day.

    Another Recipe: It treats extreme weakness and cold of the flesh, sudden wind stroke, inability to speak with the mouth shut, weakness in the limbs, spasms and acute pain, affecting the five organs, confusion, erratic emotions, with hands and feet not responding.

    Ingredients: Duhuo, Yinyi, Huangqin, each three taels; Gancao, Fangfeng, Shaoyao, Qiongyao, Mahuang, Gegeng, each two taels; Renjing one tael; three pieces of Wutuo.

    These eleven ingredients should be chewed, boiled with one dou of water and four sheng of bamboo juice, then reduce to four sheng, divided into four doses, taken three times in the day and once at night.[44p]

    　　五加酒　治肉虚坐不安席，好动，主脾病，寒气所伤。　　五加皮　枸杞皮各二升　地黄　丹参各八两　石膏　杜仲各一升　干姜四两　附子三两　　右八味，(口父)咀，以清酒二斗，渍三宿，一服七合，日再。
    　　半夏汤　治肉实，坐不安席，不能动作，喘气。主脾病，热气所加关格。除喘。　　麻黄一两　半夏　宿姜各八两　杏仁五两　细辛　橘皮各四两　石膏七两　射干二两　　右八味，(口父)咀，以水九升，煮取三升，分三服。须利下，加芒硝三两。[45p]

    Wujia Wine treats the condition of flesh being weak, feeling restless when seated, and the desire to move, primarily affecting the spleen due to damage from cold.
    Ingredients:

    • Two liters of Wujia bark
    • Eight taels each of goji berry skin, earth bulb, and salvia root
    • One liter each of gypsum and eucommia
    • Four taels of dried ginger
    • Three taels of aconite

    Combine these eight ingredients, crush, and steep in two dou of clear wine for three nights. Administer seven he for each dose, twice daily.

    Banxia Decoction is used for the condition of excess flesh, restlessness when seated, inability to move, and wheezing. It primarily affects the spleen due to an excess of heat. It alleviates wheezing.
    Ingredients:

    • One tael of ephedra
    • Eight taels each of banxia and dried ginger
    • Five taels of apricot kernel
    • Four taels each of asarum and tangerine peel
    • Seven taels of gypsum
    • Two taels of snake gourd

    Combine these eight ingredients, crush, and boil in nine liters of water to yield three liters. Divide into three doses. If a laxative effect is necessary, add three taels of Glauber's salt.[45p]

    　　地黄煎 【《中藏经》】 　解劳伤，生肌肉，进饮食，活血气，养心神。　　鹅梨汁一升　生地黄汁　杏仁汁　生姜汁　紫苏汁　薄荷汁各五升　法酒二升　沙蜜四两　　右慢火熬成膏，入后药。

    　　真武汤 【仲景】 　治悞发太阳汗，致筋惕肉瞤，以此救之。　　附子一枚，炮去皮，破八片　白茯苓　白芍药　生姜切　白朮各三两　　右五味，以水八升，煮去滓，温服七合，日三服。若咳者，加五味半合，细辛、干姜各一两。若小便利者，去茯苓。若下利者，去芍药，加干姜。若呕者，去附子，加生姜，足前成半斤。[46p]

    Di Huang Decoction 【《Zhong Zang Jing》】
    Relieves fatigue and injury, promotes muscle growth, aids digestion, invigorates blood and qi, nourishes the heart and spirit.
    One liter of goose pear juice, five liters each of fresh rehmannia juice, apricot juice, ginger juice, perilla juice, and mint juice; two liters of medicinal wine; four taels of rock sugar.
    Cook slowly until it becomes a paste, then add the following ingredients.
    Three taels of bupleurum, fragrant wood, ginseng, poria, yam, polygala, and lightly stir-fried cedar seeds, ground separately; one tael each of white atractylodes and bitter orange, wrapped in flour and baked; two taels of gentian; four taels each of platycodon and cooked rehmannia, soaked in wine, chopped, and roasted; half a tael of musk, finely ground.
    Form into pills the size of a tung seed, take twenty pills after meals with licorice decoction.

    Zhen Wu Decoction 【Zhong Jing】
    Treats excessive sweating from the Taiyang stage, causing muscle twitching and trembling.
    One piece of prepared aconite, peeled and broken into eight pieces; three taels each of white poria, white peony root, and sliced fresh ginger; and white atractylodes.
    Combine these five ingredients with eight liters of water, boil to remove dregs, and take seven sheng warm, three times a day. If coughing, add half a sheng of five-flavor fruit, and one tael each of wild ginger and dried ginger. If experiencing small, frequent bowel movements, remove poria. If there is diarrhea, remove peony, and add dried ginger. If vomiting occurs, remove aconite and add fresh ginger, making a total of half a jin.[46p]

    　　清肺饮子 【《卫生宝鉴》】 　长肌肉，补肺气，养脾胃，定心神。　　白芍五钱　人参　升麻　柴胡各四钱　天冬　麦冬各三分　陈皮二分半　黄芩　甘草生　黄蘗　甘草炙，各二分　　右十一味，(口父)咀，作一服，水二盏，煎至一盏，去滓温服，食后。汗多者，加黄芪五分。

    Lung Cleansing Decoction [from The Treasure of Hygiene]
    Strengthens the muscles, nourishes lung Qi, supports the spleen and stomach, calms the spirit.

    • White Peony Root: 5 qian
    • Ginseng: 4 qian
    • Ramie: 4 qian
    • Bupleurum: 4 qian
    • Asparagus Tuber: 3 fen
    • Ophiopogon Tuber: 3 fen
    • Dried Tangerine Peel: 2.5 fen
    • Scutellaria: 2 fen
    • Licorice (raw): 2 fen
    • Berberine: 2 fen
    • Licorice (toasted): 2 fen

    Combine these eleven ingredients, grind into a powder, make one dose with two bowls of water, boil down to one bowl, remove the dregs, and take warm after meals. For excessive sweating, add 5 fen of Astragalus.

    Fangfeng Baizhu Muli Decoction [from Zhang Zhongjing, same applies]
    Treats excessive sweating, dizziness, and muscle spasms.

    • Fang Feng
    • Stir-fried Oyster Shell
    • Bai Zhu (Atractylodes) in equal parts

    Grind these into a fine powder, each dose is 2 qian taken with wine or rice drink, two to three doses daily. Once sweating stops, take Xiao Jian Zhong Decoction.

    Xiao Jian Zhong Decoction
    For cases where sweating has ceased.

    • Cinnamon Twig: 3 liang
    • Licorice (toasted): 3 liang
    • Fresh Ginger (cut): 3 liang
    • White Peony Root: 6 liang
    • Red Dates: 12 (split)
    • Honey: 1 sheng

    Combine these six ingredients with seven sheng of water, boil down to three sheng, remove the dregs, add honey, and dissolve over low heat, take one sheng warm, three doses daily.

    Used to treat generalized numbness and lack of sensation, including numbness in the head, face, hands, feet, shoulders, back, and legs.

    Qian Hu San (Hejian)
    Used for treating severe meat-related conditions. The term "ke" (苛) indicates severity.

    Buzhong Yiqi Decoction (Dongyuan): Treats lingering illness causing emaciation, qi deficiency, numbness, weak pulse, or large but weak pulse. For cases with severe heat, use 1 qian of astragalus; 3 fen of ginseng (omit for coughing); 2 qian each of tangerine peel, blond angelica, and peasant herb; 3 qian of white atractylodes; and 5 fen of roasted licorice. Grind the ingredients and add 2 cups of water, simmer to 1 cup, adjusting water volume according to strength of qi. Take warm, away from meals. If serious injury, generally requires no more than two doses for recovery. For prolonged illness, adjust according to clinical observation.

    Easy and Simple Recipe: Treats muscle paralysis throughout the body.
    One ounce of Astragalus, five qian each of Ginseng and White Peony, one prepared Aconite, three qian of Angelica. Grind the above into a powder, refine with honey into pills the size of a wutong seed. Take three to fifty pills each time, swallowed with wine.

    Cinnamon Twig Decoction (Zhongjing): Also known as Astragalus and Cinnamon Twig Decoction, treats muscle paralysis. Warm and take seven portions, three times a day. One variation includes Ginseng.

    Exorcise Wind-Damp Qianghuo Decoction (Dongyuan): Treats unrelenting wind-damp, dizziness, and numbness. One fen of Coptis, one liang each of Qianghuo and Fangfeng; five fen each of Chaihu, Duhuo, and Licorice (roasted); seven fen of Cimicifuga; two qian of Poria; three fen each of dried Citrus peel, Huangbo, and Chuanxiong; one qian each of Cangzhu and Astragalus; two fen each of Zexie and Poria without skin. Each serving is three to five qian, boiled with two cups of water until one cup remains. Remove the dregs and warm the decoction for consumption, adjusting dosage based on one's condition.[54p]

    　　苦参丸　治肉苛。
    　　若参取粉，二两　丹参炙　沙参　人参　防风　五加皮　蒺藜炒去刺　乌蛇肉酒浸　蔓荆子　败龟板酥炙黄　虎骨酥炙黄　黑参各一两　　右为细末，用不蛀皂角一斤銼碎，以水三升，挼取汁去滓，于无油铁器内熬成膏，用炼蜜四两和丸，如梧桐子大，每服十五丸至二十丸，食后，良久夜卧。共三服，荆芥薄荷酒下。

    Kushen Pills for treating flesh deficiency.

    If using the ingredients, take two taels each of:

    • Dan Shen (Salvia miltiorrhiza) roasted,
    • Sha Shen (Glehnia littoralis),
    • Ren Shen (Ginseng),
    • Fang Feng (Saposhnikovia divaricata),
    • Wu Jia Pi (Acanthopanax),
    • Ziziphus (spiny jujube) fried to remove thorns,
    • Black Snake meat soaked in wine,
    • Man Jing Zi (vitex) baked until crisp,
    • Gui Ban (tortoise shell) fried until yellow,
    • Tiger bone fried until yellow,
    • and Black ginseng.

    Mix these into a fine powder, use 1 pound of non-bitter soap nut crushed, with 3 liters of water, extracting the juice while discarding the residue. In an oil-free iron vessel, simmer to form a paste, mix with 4 taels of honey, and shape into pills about the size of a Chinese parasol tree seed. Take 15 to 20 pills after meals, and then rest at night. Take three doses total, followed by a drink of JIng Jie (Schizonepeta), and mint wine.

    Single Prescription

    • Radix Rehmanniae (干地黄) nourishes and builds muscle, making one robust; it can be made into pills or brewed into wine for long-term use.
    • Yam (薯蓣) promotes muscle growth, supplements weakness and emaciation, making one fat; fresh yam is ground into mud and mixed with curds to make porridge, which is excellent.
    • He Shou Wu (何首乌) treats long-standing emaciation and promotes fullness; both powdered and pill forms are effective.
    • Wu Jia Pi (五加皮) is for treating weakness and can promote fullness; it can be brewed or decocted, both being effective.
    • Pine Nuts (海松子) are beneficial for emaciated individuals, helping them gain strength; consuming congee regularly is excellent.
    • Silverside Fish (鲋鱼) is good for emaciated persons to help them become robust; it can be enjoyed in soups or steamed dishes.
    • Turtle Meat (鳖肉) is effective for those who are weak and thin; the meat can be made into soup for regular consumption. Additionally, the shell can be roasted and powdered, taken with wine at a dose of one qián (3.2 grams).[55p]

    　　芋，充肌肤，令人肥白，作羹常食，甚佳。
    　　胡麻，长肌肉，肥健人，蒸曝久服，妙。
    　　大豆黄末，补劳瘦，肥健人，炼猪膏和丸服之。又鴈脂和丸服，亦可。
    　　蔓菁子，令人肥健，蒸晒作末，酒饮任下二三钱，其根作羹常食佳。
    　　韭薤俱能肥健人，作葅常食，并佳。
    　　人乳汁，治瘦瘁，令人肥白悦泽，可久服之。
    　　人胞，即胎衣也，主血气羸瘦，能肥人，蒸熟和五味食之；或合滋补药，和丸久服，尤佳。
    　　牛乳，补羸瘦，肥健人，作粥常食，佳。
    　　黄雌鸡，治羸瘦着床，能肥人，煮烂作羹服，甚良。
    　　羊肉，治瘦病，能肥健人，或煮或烧，常食，佳。
    　　黑牛髓，治瘦病，能肥人，和地黄汁白蜜等分作煎服之，佳。
    　　茶久服，去人脂，令人瘦，太肥者可服。
    　　赤小豆能瘦人，久服令人黑瘦枯燥，肥盛者可服。
    　　人太肥，欲得瘦轻健，取冬瓜长食，作羹作葅，佳。欲肥则勿食。[56p]

    Taro nourishes the skin, making one plump and fair; when made into soup and consumed regularly, it is excellent.

    Sesame promotes muscle growth and strengthens the body; steaming and drying it for prolonged consumption is wonderful.

    Yellow soybean powder replenishes those who are exhausted and thin, making them plump and strong; it can be mixed with rendered pork fat and formed into pills for consumption. Goose fat can also be mixed and consumed in pill form, which is also acceptable.

    Rutabaga seeds promote health and strength; steamed and dried into a powder, they can be taken with liquor in doses of two to three qian. Its roots can be made into soup and consumed regularly for excellent results.

    Chives and garlic both contribute to health and strength; included in dishes for regular consumption is also beneficial.

    Human milk treats emaciation and makes one plump, fair, and radiant; it can be consumed over a long period.

    The human placenta is said to enrich blood and energy; it can promote weight gain when steamed and combined with five flavors in food, or made into pills with nourishing herbs for long-term use, which is particularly beneficial.

    Cow's milk replenishes those who are thin and is wholesome; it is good when made into porridge for regular consumption.

    Yellow hen is effective for treating emaciation and can promote weight gain; boiling it into a soup is very good.

    Lamb treats thinness and promotes a strong body; it can be boiled or roasted, and consuming it regularly is beneficial.

    Black bull marrow treats thinness and promotes weight gain; it can be decocted with equal parts of rehmannia juice and white honey, which is excellent.

    Drinking tea for a long period reduces body fat and promotes weight loss; those who are overly fat may consume it.

    Red adzuki beans can help with weight loss; prolonged consumption leads to a dark, thin, and dry state, but those who are overweight may use it.

    If a person is too fat and wishes to become lean and healthy, they should consume winter melon regularly, making it into soup or dishes, which is excellent. To gain weight, one should avoid eating it.[56p]

    　　桑枝茶，逐湿令人瘦，过肥者宜久服之。
    　　昆布，下气，久服瘦人，作臛作菜常食佳。
    　　肌肉麻木疼痛，万灵膏：用甘遂二两，蓖麻子仁四两，樟脑一两，捣作饼贴之，内饮甘草汤。【《摘元方》】
    　　身体麻木：芥子末酢调涂之。 【《济生秘览》】
    　　　　针灸

    　　《素问》曰：月始生则血气始精，卫气始行；月郭满则血气实，肌肉坚；月郭空则肌肉减，经络虚，卫气去，形独居。是以因天时而调血气也，是以天寒无刺，天温无凝，月生无泻，月满无补，月郭空无治，是谓得时而调之。因天之序，盛虚之时，移光定位，正立而待之。　　病有在皮肤者，刺皮无伤肉，肉伤则内动脾，脾动则七十二日四季之月，病腹胀烦，不嗜食。　　刺皮无伤肉者，病在皮中，针入皮中，无伤肉也。　　黄帝曰：夫经脉之小大，血之多少，肤之厚薄，肉之坚脆，及腘之大小，可为度量乎？岐伯答曰：其可为度量者，取其中度也，不甚脱肉而血气不衰也。[57p]

    桑 branch tea, when consumed, expels moisture and promotes weight loss, making it suitable for those who are overweight to take for a long time.
    Kombu, which helps with digestion, is beneficial for thin individuals when consumed regularly as a dish or added to soup.
    For numbness and pain in the muscles, Wanling ointment: use two taels of Gansui, four taels of castor seed, and one tael of camphor, crush them into a cake and apply it, with an internal drink of licorice soup.
    For body numbness: use mustard powder mixed with vinegar to apply.

    According to the "Su Wen," when the moon begins to wax, the blood and qi energies start to accumulate, and the defensive qi begins to circulate; when the moon is full, the blood is abundant, and the muscles are firm; when the moon wanes, the muscles diminish, the meridians weaken, and the defensive qi disperses, leaving the body alone. Thus, blood and qi should be adjusted in accordance with the seasons. During cold weather, acupuncture should not pierce, during warm weather, should not congeal; in the waxing moon, there should be no purging; in the full moon, there should be no tonics; in the waning moon, there should be no treatments—this is called treating it in accordance with time.
    Conditions based on the sequence of nature, during times of abundance and deficiency, light should be moved to adjust positioning, standing upright and waiting for the right moment.

    For diseases of the skin, needling the skin should not injure the flesh; if the flesh is hurt, it causes internal disturbance to the spleen. If the spleen is disturbed, it leads to abdominal distension and loss of appetite, with symptoms lasting for seventy-two days across the seasons.
    Needling the skin without harming the flesh indicates that the disease is within the skin; a needle inserted into the skin does not injure the flesh.
    The Yellow Emperor asked: Can the dimensions of the meridians, the amount of blood, the thickness of the skin, the firmness of the flesh, and the size of the knees be measured? Qibo replied: What can be measured is the average; it should not excessively deplete the flesh while ensuring the blood and qi do not diminish.[57p]

    若夫度之人，痟瘦而形肉脱者，恶可以度量刺乎？审切循扪按，视其寒暑盛衰而调之，是谓因适而为之真也。　　春取络脉，夏取分腠，秋取气口，冬取经输。凡此四时，各以时为齐。络脉治皮肤，分腠治肌肉，气口治筋脉，经输治骨髓。　　春刺络脉，血气外溢，令人少气。春刺肌肉，血气环逆，令人上气。春刺筋骨，血气内着，令人腹胀。　　夏刺经脉，血气乃竭，令人解(亻亦)。夏刺肌肉，血气内却，令人善恐。夏刺筋骨，血气上逆，令人善怒。　　冬刺经脉，血气皆脱，令人目不明。冬刺络脉，内气外泄，留为大痹。冬刺肌肉，阳气竭绝，令人善忘。　　《灵枢经》曰：病在分肉间，取以圆针于病所。　　所谓三刺则谷气出者，先浅刺绝皮以出阳邪，再刺则阴邪出者少益深，绝皮致肌肉，未入分肉间也。已入分肉之间则谷气出。[58p]

    As for those who measure the body, if they are thin and emaciated, how can they accurately assess and needling them? By carefully examining and palpating, observing their seasonal changes in temperature and vitality, one adjusts accordingly; this is called acting in accordance with the true nature of things.

    In spring, one targets the collaterals; in summer, the fascial layers; in autumn, the orifices of qi; in winter, the channels and collaterals. Each of these four seasons is treated according to its own timing. The collaterals address the skin, the fascial layers treat the muscles, the orifices of qi affect the tendons, and the channels and collaterals address the bones and marrow.

    In spring, needling the collaterals causes the blood and qi to overflow outward, leading to diminished breath. Needling the muscles in spring causes blood and qi to flow in reverse, leading to shortness of breath. Needling the tendons and bones in spring causes blood and qi to stagnate inward, resulting in abdominal distension.

    In summer, needling the channels causes the blood and qi to become depleted, leading to disorientation. Needling the muscles in summer causes the blood and qi to retreat inward, resulting in anxiety. Needling the tendons and bones in summer leads to the upward reversal of blood and qi, causing anger.

    In winter, needling the channels causes the blood and qi to completely escape, leading to unclear vision. Needling the collaterals in winter causes internal qi to leak outward, resulting in great pain. Needling the muscles in winter leads to the depletion of yang qi, causing forgetfulness.

    The "Lingshu" says: When illness is located between the muscle layers, use a round needle at the site of the illness.

    The method of the three needlings to release the sourness involves first shallowly needling to break the skin to expel yang pathogens, and then deeper needling to expel the yin pathogens by penetrating further into the muscle, without yet entering the space between the muscle layers. Once penetrating into the space between the muscle layers, then the sourness is released.[58p]

    　　合谷刺者，左右鸡足针于分肉之间，以取肌痹，此脾之应也。春气在毛，夏气在皮肤，秋气在分肉，冬气在筋骨。刺此病者，各以其时为齐。故刺肥人者以秋冬之齐，刺瘦人者以春夏之齐。　　邪在脾胃，则病肌肉痛。阳气有余，阴气不足，则热中善饥。阳气不足，阴气有余，则寒中肠鸣腹痛。阴阳俱有余，若俱不足，则有寒有热，皆调于三里。　　肌寒热者，肌痛毛发焦而唇槁腊，不得汗，取三阳于下以去其血者，补足太阴以出其汗。　　风寒湿气客于外分肉之间，迫切而为沫，沫得寒则聚，聚则排分肉而分裂也。分裂则痛，痛则神归之，神归之则热，热则痛解，痛解则厥，厥则他痹发，发则如是。[59p]

    The meridian point He Gu is pricked, with needles placed between the muscle divisions on both sides, to relieve muscle stiffness, which corresponds to the spleen. Spring energy resides in the hair, summer energy in the skin, autumn energy in the muscle divisions, and winter energy in the tendons and bones. When treating these ailments, one must align with the appropriate seasonal energy. Therefore, for the obese, treatment should align with autumn and winter; for the lean, it should align with spring and summer.

    If the pathogenic factors are in the spleen and stomach, muscle pain will result. When yang energy is excessive and yin energy is insufficient, there will be heat accompanied by hunger. Conversely, when yang energy is lacking and yin energy is excessive, there will be cold, intestinal sounds, and abdominal pain. If both yin and yang energies are excessive or deficient, there will be both cold and heat, which can be balanced at the San Li point.

    For muscle pain marked by cold and heat, with hair damaged and lips dry, unable to sweat, one should tonify the three yang channels below to expel blood and supplement the taiyin to promote sweating.

    Wind, cold, and dampness invading the exterior muscle divisions lead to urgency and particular symptoms. When dampness encounters cold, it accumulates; and when it accumulates, it disrupts the muscle divisions, causing splitting. When splitting occurs, pain arises, and when the spirit returns, there is heat; the heat alleviates the pain, which in turn leads to numbness, causing further issues which manifest in the same way.[59p]

    　　黄帝问于伯高曰：何以知肉之病也？伯高曰：唇色青黄赤白黑者，病在肌肉。肉有柱，肉之柱在臂胫诸阳分肉之间，与足少阴分间。黄帝曰：取之奈何？伯高曰：百病变化，浮沉深浅，不可胜穷，各在其处。病间者浅之，甚者深之；间者少之，甚者众之。随变而调气。故曰：人之所以应土者肉也，故为之治针，必筒其身而圆其末，令无得伤肉分，伤则气得竭。　　《甲乙经》曰：咳上气喘，暴喑不能言，及舌下挟缝青脉，颈有大气，喉痹咽中干急不得息，喉中鸣，翕翕寒热，项肿肩痛，胸满，腹皮热，疟，气短哽，心痛，隐疹，头痛，面皮赤热，身肉尽不仁，夫突主之。　　寒气在分肉间，痛上下痹不仁，中渎主之。　　《医学纲目》曰：凡夏感风寒湿者，为肉痹，久而不已，则内入于脾，病四支懈惰，发咳呕汁，取太白、三里。[60p]

    The Yellow Emperor asked Bo Gao: How can one know the diseases of flesh? Bo Gao replied: The colors of the lips—blue, yellow, red, white, and black—indicate disease in the muscles. There is a structure within the flesh; this structure lies between the muscles of the arms and legs in the yang parts, and near the yin regions of the feet. The Yellow Emperor asked: How can it be treated? Bo Gao said: The myriad diseases are changeable, arising and subsiding, and are too numerous to exhaust; each has its place. Those in the superficial layer are less severe, while the deeper ones are more troublesome; the mild ones are few, while the severe ones are many. Adjust the qi according to the changes. Hence it is said: That which responds to the earth in humans is the flesh; therefore, when treating with needles, one must ensure that the body is tubular and the ends are rounded, so as to avoid injuring the flesh. If injured, the qi will be depleted.

    The "Jia Yi Classic" states: Coughing, shortness of breath, sudden loss of voice, and a blue vein beneath the tongue; with a large atmosphere around the neck, a dry and urgent throat that cannot breathe, a sound from the throat, alternating chills and fevers, swollen neck and shoulder pain, fullness in the chest, hot skin on the abdomen, malaria, shortness of breath, heart pain, rashes, headaches, red and hot facial skin, and a loss of sensitivity in the body—these indicate the primary aspects.

    Cold qi in the interstitial spaces of the muscles causes pain and numbness in both the upper and lower parts, which is managed by the Zhongdu. The "Medical Principles" states: All who suffer in summer from wind, cold, and dampness, resulting in muscle obstruction, if prolonged, will affect the spleen, resulting in weakness in the four limbs, causing coughing and vomiting of fluids; remedies include Tai Bai and San Li.[60p]

    　　　　医案

    　　《儒门事亲》曰：郾城梁贾人，年六十余，忽晓起梳发，觉左手指麻，斯须半臂麻，又一臂麻，斯须头一半麻，比及梳毕，从胁至足皆麻，大便二三日不通。往问他医，皆云风也。或药或针，皆不解，求治于戴人。戴人曰：左手三部脉皆伏，比右手小三倍，此枯濇痹也。不可纯归之风，亦有火燥相兼。乃命一涌一泄一汗，其麻立已。后以辛凉之剂调之，润燥之剂濡之，惟小指次指尚麻。戴人曰：病根已去，此余烈也，方可针溪谷。溪谷者，骨空也。一日晴和，往针之，用《灵枢》中鸡足法，向上卧针，三进三引讫，复卓针起，向下卧针送入，指间皆然。手热如火，其麻全去。昔刘河间作《原病式》，常以麻与濇同归燥门中，真知病机者也。[61p]

    Medical Case

    The "Rite of Filial Piety" states: A man from Yancheng named Liang, over sixty years old, suddenly woke up one morning to comb his hair and noticed that the fingers of his left hand were numb. In a little while, half of his arm became numb, then the other arm followed. Soon, half of his head was numb, and by the time he finished combing, he experienced numbness from his waist down to his feet. He had not had a bowel movement for two to three days. He sought the advice of doctors, who all said it was due to wind. Some prescribed medicine, others acupuncture, but nothing worked. Eventually, he sought treatment from Doctor Dai.

    Doctor Dai observed that all three pulse positions on the left hand were weak and three times smaller than those on the right hand, indicating a condition of deficiency and stagnation. It could not solely be attributed to wind; there was also accompanying dryness from heat. He prescribed a treatment involving one purge, one diuretic, and one sweating method, and the numbness immediately subsided. Afterwards, he balanced the condition with warming herbs and moistening draughts, but the little and ring fingers still showed some numbness.

    Doctor Dai commented that the root of the illness had been eradicated and that this remaining sensation was just residual heat, which could be treated with acupuncture at the gu (valley) point. The gu point is where the bone is hollow. On a sunny day, he performed the acupuncture, using the technique from the "Ling Shu" that involves the chicken foot method. He inserted needles vertically while lying on his back, advancing and retracting them three times, then removed the needles and inserted them again while lying on his stomach, applying them to the spaces between the fingers. Afterward, the hand felt hot like fire, and all numbness had ceased. In the past, Liu Hejian wrote the "Original Pathologies," often attributing numbness to dryness, thus understanding the mechanism of diseases truly well.[61p]

    　　《卫生宝鉴》曰：张抚初病时，右肩臂膊痛无主持，不能举动，多汗出，肌肉瘦，不能正卧，卧则痛甚。经曰：汗出偏沮，使人偏枯。予思《内经》云：虚与实邻，决而通之。又云：留瘦不移，节而刺之，使经络通和，血气乃复。又言：陷下者灸之，为阳气下陷入阴中，肩膊时痛，不能运动，以火导之，火引而上，补之温之。以上证皆宜灸刺。谓此先刺十二经之井穴。于四月十二日，右肩臂上肩井穴内，先针，后灸二七壮，及至疮发，渐于枯瘦处渐添肌肉，汗出少，肩臂微有力；至五月初八日再灸肩井，次于尺泽穴各灸二十八壮，引气下行，与正气相接；次日，臂膊又添气力，自能摇动矣。时值仲夏，暑热渐盛，以清肺饮子，补肺气，养脾胃，定心气。
    　　《薛己医案》曰：一产妇两手麻木，服愈风丹、天麻丸，遍身皆麻，神思倦怠，晡热作渴，自汗盗汗。余谓气血俱虚，用十全大补汤数剂，诸证悉退；又数剂而全愈。但内热，用加味逍遥散而痊。[62p]

    The "Treasures of Health" states: When Zhang Fuchu was ill, he experienced pain in his right shoulder and arm that could not be controlled. He was unable to move, sweated excessively, the muscles were emaciated, and he could not lie down properly as it caused more pain. The classic states: Excessive sweating leads to weakness, causing a person to become emaciated. I reflect on the "Inner Canon," which says that deficiency and excess are neighbors, and one can resolve and connect them. It also states: If one remains emaciated and stagnant, one must use acupuncture and moxibustion to unblock and harmonize the meridians, allowing blood and energy to recover. It mentions that if there is sinking energy, moxibustion should be applied, as vital energy has descended into the Yin. When the shoulder pains intermittently and cannot move, one should guide it with fire; fire leads upwards, thus replenishing and warming. All these symptoms are suitable for acupuncture and moxibustion. It is said that one should first puncture the Jing points of the twelve meridians. On April 12, I first needled the Jianjing point on the upper shoulder of the right arm, then applied moxibustion for fifteen sessions, whereupon sore areas began to emerge, and gradually muscle was added to the lean areas, sweating decreased, and the shoulder and arm regained some strength. By May 8, I applied moxibustion again at Jianjing and then at the Chize point, each for twenty-eight sessions, directing energy downward to connect with the righteous energy. The next day, the arm again gained strength and could move. It was mid-summer, with increasing heat, so I prescribed Qingfei Yin to tonify lung energy, nourish the spleen and stomach, and calm the heart.

    In "Xue Ji's Medical Records," it is stated: A parturient woman experienced numbness in both hands. After taking Yufeng Dan and Tianma Pills, she felt numbness all over the body, was lethargic, thirsty during the evening, and experienced spontaneous sweating and night sweats. I prescribed several doses of Shenqi Dabu Decoction, after which all symptoms receded. After a few more doses, she recovered completely. However, because of internal heat, I used Jiawei Xiaoyao Powder for her cure.[62p]

    　　一妇人元气素虚，劳则体麻发热，痰气上攻，或用乌药顺气散、祛风化痰丸之类，肢体痿软，痰涎自出，面色痿黄，形体倦怠，而脾肺二脉虚甚，此虚而类风也。朝用补中益气汤，夕用十全大补汤，渐愈。又用加味归脾汤调理，寻愈。
    　　《证治准绳》曰：李正臣夫人病，诊得六脉中俱弦，洪缓相合，按之无力，弦在其上，是风热下陷入阴中，阳道不行。其证闭目则浑身麻木，昼减而夜甚，觉而目开则麻木渐退，久则绝止，常开其目，此证不作。惧其麻木，不敢合眼，故不得眠。身体皆重，时有痰嗽，觉胸中常是有痰而不利，时烦燥，气短促而喘，肌肤充盛，饮食大小便如常。惟畏麻木，不敢合眼为最苦。观其色脉，形病相应而不逆。《内经》曰：阳病，开目而动，轻；阴病，闭目而静，重。又云：诸脉皆属于目。[63p]

    A woman initially suffered from a deficiency of vital energy. When fatigued, her body became numb and warm, with phlegm and qi rising to attack. She was treated with remedies like Wuyao Shunqi Powder and Qufeng Huatan Pill. Her limbs were weak and her phlegm and saliva were spontaneously expelled. She had a sallow complexion and felt fatigued, with her spleen and lungs notably weak, indicating deficiency resembling wind. She improved gradually with the morning use of Bu Zhong Yi Qi Decoction and evening use of Shi Quan Da Bu Decoction. Eventually, she was treated with a modified Gui Pi Decoction and recovered.

    The "Zheng Zhi Zhun Sheng" states: Mrs. Li Zhengchen was diagnosed with a pulse that was thin and taut, both full and slow, with no strength upon palpation. The tautness was at the superficial level, indicating wind-heat sinking into the yin, obstructing the yang path. Her symptoms included complete body numbness with closed eyes, which was less severe in the daytime and worse at night; upon awakening and opening her eyes, the numbness gradually receded, and if prolonged, it would stop. She kept her eyes open due to fear of numbness, causing insomnia. Her body felt heavy, with occasional phlegmatic cough, a constant sensation of phlegm in her chest that was not easily expelled, and intermittent agitation with shortness of breath and wheezing. Her skin appeared swollen, but her appetite and bowel movements were normal. The greatest suffering was the fear of numbness and the inability to close her eyes. Observing her color and pulse, her symptoms matched the state of her illness without contradiction. The "Inner Canon" states: In yang conditions, opening the eyes and moving is light; in yin conditions, closing the eyes and resting is heavy. It further states: All pulses are related to the eyes.[63p]

    《灵枢》曰：开目则阳道行，阳气遍布周身；闭目则阳道闭而不行。如昼夜之分，知其阳衰而阴旺也。且麻木为风，虽三尺之童，皆以为然，细校之则非。如久坐而起，亦有麻木。假如为绳紧缚之人，释之觉麻木作而不敢动，久则自已。以此验之，非风邪，乃气不行也。不须治风，当补其肺中之气，则麻木自去矣。知其经脉阴火乘其阳分，火动于中，为麻木也，当兼去阴火则愈矣。时痰嗽者，秋凉在外，湿在上作也，当实其皮毛以温剂。身重脉缓者，湿气伏匿而作也，时见躁作，当升阳助气益血，微泻阴火去湿，通行经脉，调其阴阳则已，非五脏六腑之本有邪也。补气升阳和中汤主之。[64p]

    The “Lingshu” states: When the eyes are opened, the yang pathway operates, and the yang energy spreads throughout the body; when the eyes are closed, the yang pathway is blocked and does not operate. This is like the division between day and night, understanding that the yang declines while the yin flourishes. Furthermore, numbness is caused by wind; even a three-foot-tall child understands this, but upon closer examination, it is not true. For instance, one becomes numb after sitting for a long time. If a person is tightly bound by a rope, once released, they may feel numb but dare not move; after a while, they adapt. Observing this, it is clear that it is not an invasion of wind, but rather that the energy is stagnant. There is no need to treat for wind; one should tonify the lung's energy, and then the numbness will dissipate. Understanding that the yin fire within the meridians affects the yang aspect, with internal movement causing numbness, one should also eliminate the yin fire to achieve recovery. When there is phlegm and coughing, it is due to the coolness of autumn on the outside and dampness causing discomfort. One should warm the skin with warming medicinals. When the body feels heavy and the pulse is slow, it indicates trapped dampness. When an anxious sensation appears, one should raise the yang, support the qi, and enrich the blood, subtly drain the yin fire and eliminate dampness, allowing the meridians to flow and balancing the yin and yang. It does not signify an innate evil in the five organs and six bowels. The remedy is to supplement qi, elevate yang, and harmonize.[64p]

    　　李夫人立冬严霜时得病，四肢无力痿厥，乃湿热在下焦也。酢心者，是浊气不降，欲满也。合眼麻木者，阳道不行也。开眼不麻木者，目开助阳道，故降寒之气少退也。头旋眩运者，风气下陷于血分，不伸越而作也。温经除湿汤主之。
    　　大理少卿韩珠泉遍身麻痹，不能举动，求治于予。予以神效黄芪汤方加减授之，用芪一两二钱，参、芍各六钱。他称是，一服减半。彼欲速效，遂并两剂为一服之，旬日而病如失矣。予以元气初复，宜静以养之，完固而后可出。渠不能从，盛夏遽出，朝见谒客，劳烦屡日，偶从朝房出上马，忽欲坠仆，从者扶至邸寓，邀予视之，予辞不治，数日而殁。
    [65p]

    During the severe winter frost, Lady Li fell ill, with her limbs weak and paralyzed, indicating damp heat in the lower body. The bitter heart indicates that the turbid qi does not descend and is accumulating. If the eyes are numb when closed, it signifies that the yang pathways are not functioning. If the eyes are not numb when open, it indicates that the opening of the eyes aids the yang pathways, thus slightly alleviating the cold qi. Dizziness and spinning in the head indicate that the wind qi has sunk into the blood aspect, and it arises without stretching out. The "Warming the Meridians and Eliminating Dampness Decoction" is prescribed for this condition.

    The Deputy Minister of Dali, Han Zhuquan, experienced complete paralysis and could not move, seeking treatment from me. I provided him with a modified version of the "Miraculous Efficacy Astragalus Decoction," using one liang and two qian of astragalus, and six qian each of ginseng and peony. The rest of the ingredients were similar, and one dose was reduced by half. He wanted immediate results, so he combined two doses into one, and within ten days, his illness seemed to vanish. I advised him that with his original qi beginning to recover, he should rest to nourish it, and only after it became solid should he go out. He could not follow this advice and suddenly went out during the heat of summer, attending to guests and becoming fatigued over several days. One day, while exiting the morning chamber and mounting a horse, he unexpectedly nearly fell over. Companions assisted him to the guesthouse and invited me to examine him, but I declined treatment. A few days later, he passed away.[65p]
